#c9ffd9;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-1" title="ISO 639-1">ISO 639-1</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><span class="plainlinks"><a class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?iso_639_1=es" rel="nofollow">es</a></span></code></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-2" title="ISO 639-2">ISO 639-2</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i></th><td class="infobox-data" scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><a href="/wiki/Linguasphere_Observatory" title="Linguasphere Observatory">Linguasphere</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code>51-AAA-b</code></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hispanophone_global_world_map_language.svg"><img alt="Hispanophone global world map language.svg" data-file-height="282" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="121" style="text-align:left;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#001E60; color:white;"> </span> Spanish as official language.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#004F96; color:white;"> </span> Unofficial, but spoken by more than 25% of the population.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#0086D8; color:black;"> </span> Unofficial, but spoken by 10–20% of the population.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#78C0FF; color:black;"> </span> Unofficial, but spoken by 5–9% of the population.</div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#B8E1FF; color:black;"> </span> Spanish-based creole languages spoken.</div></div></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-below noprint selfref" colspan="2" style="background-color:#E7E7FF;padding:0.3em 0.5em;text-align:left;line-height:1.3;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA#Rendering_issues" title="Help:IPA">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">Help:IPA</a>.</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Spanish</b> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Espanolpronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0d/Es-espa%C3%B1ol.oga" title="Es-español.oga"><i>español</i></a></span></span> or <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es_castellano_001.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Es_castellano_001.ogg" title="Es castellano 001.ogg"><i>castellano</i></a></span></span>, <b>Castilian</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance language</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-European_language_family" title="Indo-European language family">Indo-European language family</a>  that evolved from colloquial <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> spoken in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> of <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>. Today, it is a <a href="/wiki/World_language" title="World language">global language</a> with more than 500 million native speakers, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>. Spanish is the official language of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_Spanish_is_an_official_language" title="List of countries where Spanish is an official language">20 countries</a>. It is the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">second-most spoken native language</a> after <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-size_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-size-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_total_number_of_speakers" title="List of languages by total number of speakers">fourth-most spoken language</a> overall after <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, Mandarin Chinese, and <a href="/wiki/Hindustani_language" title="Hindustani language">Hindustani</a> (Hindi-Urdu); and the world's most widely spoken <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance language</a>. The largest population of native speakers is in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish is part of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">Ibero-Romance group of languages</a>, which evolved from several dialects of <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> in Iberia after the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> in the 5th century. The oldest <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> texts with traces of Spanish come from mid-northern Iberia in the 9th century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and the first systematic written use of the language happened in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toledo_(Spain)" title="Toledo (Spain)">Toledo</a>, a prominent city of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>, in the 13th century. Spanish colonialism in the Early Modern Period spurred on the introduction of the language to overseas locations, most notably to the Americas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a Romance language, Spanish is a descendant of Latin, and has one of the smaller degrees of difference from it (about 20%) alongside <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">Sardinian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Around 75% of modern Spanish vocabulary is derived from Latin, including Latin borrowings from Ancient Greek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Alongside English and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, it is also one of the most taught foreign languages throughout the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Spanish does not feature prominently as a scientific language; however, it is better represented in areas like <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_sciences" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Spanish is also the third most used language on internet websites after English and Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish is one of the <a href="/wiki/Official_languages_of_the_United_Nations" title="Official languages of the United Nations">six official languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and it is also used as an official language by the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_Spanish_is_an_official_language#International_organizations_where_Spanish_is_official" title="List of countries where Spanish is an official language">many other international organizations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_of_the_language_and_etymology">Name of the language and etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name of the language and etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_given_to_the_Spanish_language" title="Names given to the Spanish language">Names given to the Spanish language</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="922" data-file-width="694" decoding="async" height="372" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png/280px-Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png/420px-Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png/560px-Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Castellano-Espa%C3%B1ol-es.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map indicating places where the language is called <i>castellano</i> (in red) or <i>español</i> (in blue)</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name_of_the_language">Name of the language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Name of the language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Spain and in some other parts of the Spanish-speaking world, Spanish is called not only <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/espa%C3%B1ol#Spanish" title="wikt:español">español</a></i></span> but also <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/castellano#Spanish" title="wikt:castellano">castellano</a></i></span> (Castilian), the language from the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a>, contrasting it with other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">languages spoken in Spain</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan_Language" title="Occitan Language">Occitan</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">Spanish Constitution of 1978</a> uses the term <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castellano</i></span> to define the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the whole Spanish State, in contrast to <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">las demás lenguas españolas</i></span> (lit. "the other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">Spanish languages</a>"). Article III reads as follows:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">El castellano es la lengua española oficial del Estado. ... Las demás lenguas españolas serán también oficiales en las respectivas Comunidades Autónomas...</i></span><br/>
Castilian is the official Spanish language of the State. ... The other Spanish languages shall also be official in their respective Autonomous Communities...</p></blockquote>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">Royal Spanish Academy</a> (<i>Real Academia Española</i>), on the other hand, currently uses the term <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span> in its publications. However, from 1713 to 1923, it called the language <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castellano</i></span>.
</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Diccionario_panhisp%C3%A1nico_de_dudas" title="Diccionario panhispánico de dudas">Diccionario panhispánico de dudas</a></i></span> (a language guide published by the Royal Spanish Academy) states that, although the Royal Spanish Academy prefers to use the term <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span> in its publications when referring to the Spanish language, both terms—<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castellano</i></span>—are regarded as synonymous and equally valid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castellano</i></span> is related to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Castile</a> (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Castilla</i></span> or archaically <span title="Old Spanish-language text"><i lang="osp">Castiella</i></span>), the kingdom where the language was originally spoken. The name of Castile, in turn, is usually assumed to be derived from <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castillo</i></span> ('castle').
</p><p>In the middle ages, the language spoken in Castile was generically referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Romance</i></span> and later also as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Lengua vulgar</i></span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espania_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-espania-17">[17]</a></sup> Later in the period, it gained geographical specification as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Romance castellano</i></span> ("romanz castellano", "romanz de Castiella"), "lenguaje de Castiella", and ultimately simply as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">castellano</i></span> (noun).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espania_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-espania-17">[17]</a></sup>
</p><p>Different etymologies have been suggested for the term <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span> (Spanish). According to the Royal Spanish Academy, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span> derives from the <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> word <i>espaignol</i> and that, in turn, derives from the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> <span title="Latin-language text">*<i lang="la">hispaniolus</i></span> ('from Hispania').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> was the Roman name for the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>.
</p><p>There are other hypotheses apart from the one suggested by the Royal Spanish Academy. Spanish philologist <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Ramón Menéndez Pidal">Menéndez Pidal</a> suggested that the classic <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">hispanus</i></span> or <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">hispanicus</i></span> took the suffix <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">-one</i></span> from <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>, as it happened with other words such as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">bretón</i></span> (Breton) or <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sajón</i></span> (Saxon). The word <span title="Latin-language text">*<i lang="la">hispanione</i></span> evolved into the <a href="/wiki/Old_Spanish" title="Old Spanish">Old Spanish</a> <span title="Old Spanish-language text"><i lang="osp">españón</i></span>, eventually becoming <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">español</i></span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Spanish_language" title="History of the Spanish language">History of the Spanish language</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CartulariosValpuesta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="145" data-file-width="255" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/CartulariosValpuesta.jpg/220px-CartulariosValpuesta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/CartulariosValpuesta.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CartulariosValpuesta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Visigothic <a href="/wiki/Cartularies_of_Valpuesta" title="Cartularies of Valpuesta">Cartularies of Valpuesta</a>, written in a late form of Latin, were declared in 2010 by the Royal Spanish Academy as the record of the earliest words written in Castilian, predating those of the <a href="/wiki/Glosas_Emilianenses" title="Glosas Emilianenses">Glosas Emilianenses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Like the other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romance_language" title="Romance language">Romance languages</a>, the Spanish language evolved from <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>, which here was brought to the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Romans</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>, beginning in 210 BC. Several pre-Roman languages (also called <a href="/wiki/Paleohispanic_languages" title="Paleohispanic languages">Paleohispanic languages</a>)—some distantly related to Latin as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-European_language" title="Indo-European language">Indo-European languages</a>, and some that are not related at all—were previously spoken in the Iberian Peninsula. These languages included <a href="/wiki/Proto-Basque_language" title="Proto-Basque language">Proto-Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberian_language" title="Iberian language">Iberian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lusitanian_language" title="Lusitanian language">Lusitanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtiberian_language" title="Celtiberian language">Celtiberian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gallaecian_language" title="Gallaecian language">Gallaecian</a>.
</p><p>The first documents to show traces of what is today regarded as the precursor of modern Spanish are from the 9th century. Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> and into the <a href="/wiki/Modern_era" title="Modern era">modern era</a>, the most important <a href="/wiki/Language_contact" title="Language contact">influences</a> on the Spanish lexicon came from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>—<a href="/wiki/Mozarabic_language" title="Mozarabic language">Mozarabic</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andalusi_Romance" title="Andalusi Romance">Andalusi Romance</a>), <a href="/wiki/Navarro-Aragonese" title="Navarro-Aragonese">Navarro-Aragonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonese_language" title="Leonese language">Leonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>, and later, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>. Spanish also <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">borrowed</a> a considerable number of words from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>, as well as a minor influence from the Germanic <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic language</a> through the migration of tribes and a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visigoth" title="Visigoth">Visigoth</a> rule in Iberia. In addition, many more words were borrowed from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a> through the influence of written language and the liturgical language of the Church. The loanwords were taken from both <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">Classical Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Latin" title="Renaissance Latin">Renaissance Latin</a>, the form of Latin in use at that time.
</p><p>According to the theories of <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Ramón Menéndez Pidal">Ramón Menéndez Pidal</a>, local <a href="/wiki/Sociolect" title="Sociolect">sociolects</a> of Vulgar Latin evolved into Spanish, in the north of Iberia, in an area centered in the city of <a href="/wiki/Burgos" title="Burgos">Burgos</a>, and this dialect was later brought to the city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toledo_(Spain)" title="Toledo (Spain)">Toledo</a>, where the written standard of Spanish was first developed, in the 13th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Penny1p16_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Penny1p16-20">[20]</a></sup> In this formative stage, Spanish developed a strongly differing variant from its close cousin, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonese_Language" title="Leonese Language">Leonese</a>, and, according to some authors, was distinguished by a heavy Basque influence (see <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">Iberian Romance languages</a>). This distinctive dialect spread to southern Spain with the advance of the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i></span>, and meanwhile gathered a sizable lexical influence from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Al-Andalus</a>, much of it indirectly, through the Romance <a href="/wiki/Mozarabic_language" title="Mozarabic language">Mozarabic dialects</a> (some 4,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>-derived words, make up around 8% of the language today).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The written standard for this new language was developed in the cities of <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a>, in the 13th to 16th centuries, and <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, from the 1570s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Penny1p16_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Penny1p16-20">[20]</a></sup>
</p><p>The development of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">Spanish sound system</a> from that of <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> exhibits most of the changes that are typical of <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">Western Romance languages</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenition</a> of intervocalic consonants (thus Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r920966791">.mw-parser-output span.smallcaps{font-variant:small-caps}.mw-parser-output span.smallcaps-smaller{font-size:85%}</style><span class="smallcaps">vīta</span></i></span> &gt; Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">vida</i></span>). The <a href="/wiki/Vowel_breaking" title="Vowel breaking">diphthongization</a> of Latin stressed short <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">e</span> and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">o</span>—which occurred in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable_coda" title="Syllable coda">open syllables</a> in French and Italian, but not at all in Catalan or Portuguese—is found in both open and closed syllables in Spanish, as shown in the following table:
</p>

</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="806" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/220px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/330px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif/440px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe-en.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chronological map showing linguistic evolution in southwest Europe</div></div></div>
<p>Spanish is marked by <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(sound_change)" title="Palatalization (sound change)">palatalization</a> of the Latin double consonants (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geminate" title="Geminate">geminates</a>) <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">nn</span> and <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">ll</span> (thus Latin
<span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">annum</span></i></span> &gt; Spanish <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">año</i></span>, and Latin <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r920966791" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><span class="smallcaps">anellum</span></i></span> &gt; Spanish
<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">anillo</i></span>).
</p><p>The consonant written <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">u</i></span> or <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">v</i></span> in Latin and pronounced <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[w]</span> in Classical Latin had probably "<a href="/wiki/Fortition" title="Fortition">fortified</a>" to a bilabial fricative <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/β/</span> in Vulgar Latin. In early Spanish (but not in Catalan or Portuguese) it merged with the consonant written <i>b</i> (a bilabial with plosive and fricative allophones). In modern Spanish, there is <a href="/wiki/Betacism" title="Betacism">no difference</a> between the pronunciation of orthographic <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">b</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">v</i></span>, with some exceptions in Caribbean Spanish.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Typical of Spanish (as also of neighboring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gascon_language" title="Gascon language">Gascon</a> extending as far north as the <a href="/wiki/Gironde_estuary" title="Gironde estuary">Gironde estuary</a>, and found in a small area of <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a>), attributed by some scholars to a Basque <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substratum" title="Substratum">substratum</a> was the mutation of Latin initial <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">f</i></span> into <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">h-</i></span> whenever it was followed by a vowel that did not diphthongize. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">h-</i></span>, still preserved in spelling, is now silent in most varieties of the language, although in some Andalusian and Caribbean dialects it is still aspirated in some words. Because of borrowings from Latin and from neighboring Romance languages, there are many <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">f</i></span>-/<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">h</i></span>-<a href="/wiki/Doublet_(linguistics)" title="Doublet (linguistics)">doublets</a> in modern Spanish: <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fernando</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Hernando</i></span> (both Spanish for "Ferdinand"), <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ferrero</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">herrero</i></span> (both Spanish for "smith"), <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">fierro</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hierro</i></span> (both Spanish for "iron"), and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">fondo</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hondo</i></span> (both Spanish for "deep", but <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">fondo</i></span> means "bottom" while <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hondo</i></span> means "deep"); <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hacer</i></span> (Spanish for "to make") is <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognate</a> to the root word of <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">satisfacer</i></span> ("to satisfy"), and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hecho</i></span> ("made") is similarly cognate to the root word of <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">satisfecho</i></span> ("satisfied").
</p><p>Compare the examples in the following table:
