<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="1220" decoding="async" height="251" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg/170px-Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg/255px-Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg/340px-Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Juan_de_Z%C3%BA%C3%B1iga_dibujo_con_orla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Nebrija" title="Antonio de Nebrija">Antonio de Nebrija</a>, author of <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Gram%C3%A1tica_de_la_lengua_castellana" title="Gramática de la lengua castellana">Gramática de la lengua castellana</a></i></span>, the first grammar of a modern European language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In the 15th and 16th centuries, Spanish underwent a dramatic change in the pronunciation of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sibilant_consonants" title="Sibilant consonants">sibilant consonants</a>, known in Spanish as the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reajuste_de_las_sibilantes_del_idioma_espa%C3%B1ol" title="es:Reajuste de las sibilantes del idioma español">reajuste de las sibilantes</a></i></span>, which resulted in the distinctive <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Velar" title="Velar">velar</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[x]</span> pronunciation of the letter ⟨j⟩ and—in a large part of Spain—the characteristic <a href="/wiki/Interdental_consonant" title="Interdental consonant">interdental</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[θ]</span> ("th-sound") for the letter ⟨z⟩ (and for ⟨c⟩ before ⟨e⟩ or ⟨i⟩). See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Spanish#Modern_development_of_the_Old_Spanish_sibilants" title="History of Spanish">History of Spanish (Modern development of the Old Spanish sibilants)</a> for details.
</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Gram%C3%A1tica_de_la_lengua_castellana" title="Gramática de la lengua castellana">Gramática de la lengua castellana</a></i></span>, written in <a href="/wiki/Salamanca" title="Salamanca">Salamanca</a> in 1492 by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_de_Nebrija" title="Antonio de Nebrija">Elio Antonio de Nebrija</a>, was the first grammar written for a modern European language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> According to a popular anecdote, when Nebrija presented it to <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Queen Isabella I</a>, she asked him what was the use of such a work, and he answered that language is the instrument of empire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In his introduction to the grammar, dated 18 August 1492, Nebrija wrote that "... language was always the companion of empire."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>From the 16th century onwards, the language was taken to the Spanish-discovered <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">America</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a> via <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization of America</a>. <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a>, author of <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">Don Quixote</a></i>, is such a well-known reference in the world that Spanish is often called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">la lengua de Cervantes</i></span> ("the language of Cervantes").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 20th century, Spanish was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, and to areas of the United States that had not been part of the Spanish Empire, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_Harlem" title="Spanish Harlem">Spanish Harlem</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. For details on borrowed words and other external influences upon Spanish, see <a href="/wiki/Influences_on_the_Spanish_language" title="Influences on the Spanish language">Influences on the Spanish language</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_distribution">Geographical distribution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geographical distribution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Hispanophone" title="Hispanophone">Hispanophone</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="441" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png/220px-Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png/330px-Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png/440px-Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geographical_places_of_the_spanish_language.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geographical distribution of the Spanish language <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#800000; color:white;"> </span> Official or co-official language</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#D40000; color:white;"> </span> 1,000,000+</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FF8080; color:black;"> </span> 100,000+</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFD5D5; color:black;"> </span> 20,000+</div> <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Active learning of Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></div></div></div></div>
<p>Spanish is the primary language in 20 countries worldwide. As of 2020, it is estimated that about 463 million people speak Spanish as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_language" title="Native language">native language</a>, making it the second <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">most spoken language by number of native speakers</a>. An additional 75 million speak Spanish as a second or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_as_a_foreign_language" title="Spanish as a foreign language">foreign language</a>, making it the fourth most spoken language in the world overall after English, Mandarin Chinese, and Hindi with a total number of 538 million speakers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Spanish is also the third <a href="/wiki/Languages_used_on_the_Internet" title="Languages used on the Internet">most used language on the Internet</a>, after English and Chinese.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Spanish" title="Peninsular Spanish">Peninsular Spanish</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="570" decoding="async" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg/220px-Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg/330px-Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg/440px-Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Knowledge_of_Spanish_in_European_Union.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of people who self reportedly know enough Spanish to hold a conversation, in the EU, 2005 <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#554400; color:white;"> </span> Native country</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#AA8800; color:black;"> </span> More than 8.99%</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#E5B700; color:black;"> </span> Between 4% and 8.99%</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFDD55; color:black;"> </span> Between 1% and 3.99%</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FFEEAA; color:black;"> </span> Less than 1%</div></div></div></div>
<p>Spanish is the official language of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the country after which it is named and from which it originated. Other European territories in which it is also widely spoken include <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish is also spoken by immigrant communities in other European countries, such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Spanish is an official language of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Americas">Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hispanic_America">Hispanic America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Hispanic America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Americas" title="Spanish language in the Americas">Spanish language in the Americas</a></div>
<p>Today, the majority of the Spanish speakers live in <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic America</a>. Nationally, Spanish is the official language—either <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i>—of <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> (co-official with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guarani</a>, and 34 other languages), <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (co-official with 63 indigenous languages), <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> (co-official with <a href="/wiki/Guarani_language" title="Guarani language">Guaraní</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> (co-official with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_language" title="Quechua language">Quechua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a>, and "the other indigenous languages"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup>), <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> (co-official with English),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States" title="Spanish language in the United States">Spanish language in the United States</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_Spanish" title="New Mexican Spanish">New Mexican Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isle%C3%B1o_Spanish" title="Isleño Spanish">Isleño Spanish</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="959" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg/300px-Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg/450px-Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg/600px-Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_spoken_at_home_in_the_United_States_2019.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Percentage of the U.S. population aged 5 and over who speaks Spanish at home in 2019, by states.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the 2020 census, over 60 million people of the U.S. population were of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic American</a> by origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In turn, 41.8 million people in the United States aged five or older speak Spanish at home, or about 13% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The Spanish language has a long history of presence in the United States due to early Spanish and, later, Mexican administration over territories now forming the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">southwestern states</a>, also <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">Louisiana</a> ruled by Spain from 1762 to 1802, as well as <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, which was Spanish territory until 1821, and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> which was Spanish until 1898.
</p><p>Spanish is by far the most common second language in the country, with over 50 million total speakers if non-native or second-language speakers are included.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Más_'speak_spanish'_que_en_España_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Más_'speak_spanish'_que_en_España-37">[37]</a></sup> While English is the de facto national language of the country, Spanish is often used in public services and notices at the federal and state levels. Spanish is also used in administration in the state of <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The language has a strong influence in major metropolitan areas such as those of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_area" title="Greater Los Angeles area">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miami_metropolitan_area" title="Miami metropolitan area">Miami</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Antonio_metropolitan_area" title="San Antonio metropolitan area">San Antonio</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_metropolitan_area" title="New York metropolitan area">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dallas%E2%80%93Fort_Worth_metroplex" title="Dallas–Fort Worth metroplex">Dallas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Tucson" title="Greater Tucson">Tucson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_metropolitan_area" title="Phoenix metropolitan area">Phoenix</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Sun_Corridor" title="Arizona Sun Corridor">Arizona Sun Corridor</a>, as well as more recently, <a href="/wiki/Chicago_metropolitan_area" title="Chicago metropolitan area">Chicago</a>, <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Boston" title="Greater Boston">Boston</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Denver" title="Greater Denver">Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Houston" title="Greater Houston">Houston</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Indianapolis" title="Greater Indianapolis">Indianapolis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Philadelphia" title="Greater Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Cleveland" title="Greater Cleveland">Cleveland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Salt_Lake_City" title="Greater Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Atlanta" title="Greater Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Nashville" title="Greater Nashville">Nashville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greater_Orlando" title="Greater Orlando">Orlando</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Tampa" title="Greater Tampa">Tampa</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Raleigh" title="Greater Raleigh">Raleigh</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area">Baltimore-Washington, D.C.</a> due to 20th- and 21st-century immigration.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rest_of_the_Americas">Rest of the Americas</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rest of the Americas">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although Spanish has no official recognition in the former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_overseas_territories" title="British overseas territories">British colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> (known until 1973 as <a href="/wiki/British_Honduras" title="British Honduras">British Honduras</a>) where English is the sole official language, according to the 2010 census it was then spoken natively by 45% of the population and 56.6% of the total population were able to speak the language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to their proximity to Spanish-speaking countries, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> has implemented Spanish language teaching into its education system. The Trinidad government launched the <i>Spanish as a First Foreign Language</i> (SAFFL) initiative in March 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to sharing most of its borders with Spanish-speaking countries, the creation of <a href="/wiki/Mercosur" title="Mercosur">Mercosur</a> in the early 1990s induced a favorable situation for the promotion of Spanish language teaching in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEValleVilla2006376_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEValleVilla2006376-41">[41]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cuny_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-cuny-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/National_Congress_of_Brazil" title="National Congress of Brazil">National Congress of Brazil</a> approved a bill, signed into law by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">President</a>, making it mandatory for <a href="/wiki/School" title="School">schools</a> to offer Spanish as an alternative foreign language course in both public and private secondary schools in Brazil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> In September 2016 this law was revoked by <a href="/wiki/Michel_Temer" title="Michel Temer">Michel Temer</a> after <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">impeachment of Dilma Rousseff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> In many border towns and villages along Paraguay and Uruguay, a <a href="/wiki/Mixed_language" title="Mixed language">mixed language</a> known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riverense_Portu%C3%B1ol" title="Riverense Portuñol">Portuñol</a> is spoken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Africa">Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-Saharan_Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sub-Saharan Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Equatoguinean_Spanish" title="Equatoguinean Spanish">Equatoguinean Spanish</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malabo_08207.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Malabo_08207.JPG/220px-Malabo_08207.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Malabo_08207.JPG/330px-Malabo_08207.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Malabo_08207.JPG/440px-Malabo_08207.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Malabo_08207.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish language signage in <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, capital city of <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a> is the only Sub-Saharan Spanish-speaking country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> where it was introduced by the 19th century once the Spain's control over its colonies in the gulf of Guinea acquired in 1778 consolidated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-subsahara_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-subsahara-47">[47]</a></sup> Enshrined in the constitution as an official language (alongside French and Portuguese), Spanish prominently features in the Equatoguinean education system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Whereas Spanish is not the mother tongue of any of its speakers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> Equatorial Guinea features a higher proportion of proficient speakers of the colonizing language relative to the respective metropolitan languages in other West and Central African nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">Instituto Cervantes</a>, 87.7% of the population is fluent in Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> It vies with <a href="/wiki/Fang_language" title="Fang language">Fang</a> as lingua franca in <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">Río Muni</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Pichinglis" title="Pichinglis">Pichi</a> creole remains so in <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">Bioko</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELipski2004116–117_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELipski2004116–117-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish is spoken by very small communities in <a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> due to Cuban influence from the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> and in <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> among South Sudanese natives that relocated to Cuba during the Sudanese wars and returned for their country's independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="North_Africa_and_Macaronesia">North Africa and Macaronesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: North Africa and Macaronesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Canarian_Spanish" title="Canarian Spanish">Canarian Spanish</a></div>
<p>Spanish is also spoken in the territories of Spain in Africa, for all intents and purposes the cities of <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, located in the Atlantic Ocean some 100 km (62 mi) off the northwest of the African mainland. The Spanish spoken in the Canary Islands (population over two million), traces its origins back to the <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Canary_Islands" title="Conquest of the Canary Islands">Castilian conquest in the 15th century</a>, and, in addition to a resemblance to Western Andalusian speech patterns, it also features strong influence from the Spanish varieties spoken in the Americas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> which in turn have also been influenced historically by Canarian Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish has been a vernacular language in Ceuta and Melilla (combined population over 150 thousand) since the early modern period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVicente201161_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVicente201161-56">[56]</a></sup> The varieties of Spanish spoken in Ceuta and Melilla are closer to, respectively, Western and Eastern Andalusian speech patterns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Likewise, in line with the sociolinguistic situation in the adjoining territory, Spanish is respectively in contact with <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_Arabic" title="Moroccan Arabic">Moroccan Arabic</a> (Ceuta) and <a href="/wiki/Tarifit" title="Tarifit">Riffian</a> (Melilla).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVicente201162_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVicente201162-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>While far from the heyday of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_protectorate_in_Morocco" title="Spanish protectorate in Morocco">Spanish protectorate in Morocco</a>, there are some presence of the Spanish language in the north of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, stemming for example from the availability of certain Spanish-language media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVicente201167_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVicente201167-59">[59]</a></sup> Many northern Moroccans have rudimentary knowledge of Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVicente201167_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVicente201167-59">[59]</a></sup> Spanish has also presence in the education system of the country (either by means of selected education centres running the Spain's education system, primarily located in the North, and the availability of Spanish as foreign language subject in secondary education).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVicente201167_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVicente201167-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a>, formerly <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Sahara" title="Spanish Sahara">Spanish Sahara</a>, a primarily <a href="/wiki/Hassaniya_Arabic" title="Hassaniya Arabic">Hassaniya Arabic</a>-speaking territory, Spanish was officially spoken as the language of the colonial administration during the late 19th and 20th centuries. Today, Spanish is present in the partially-recognized <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_Arab_Democratic_Republic" title="Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic">Sahrawi Arab Democratic Republic</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps" title="Sahrawi refugee camps">Sahrawi refugee camps in Tindouf</a> (<a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>), where the Spanish-language teaching is largely preserved by Cuban educators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The number of Spanish speakers is unknown.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2022)">failed verification</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p><p>Spanish is also an official language of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Asia">Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Chavacano" title="Chavacano">Chavacano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines" title="Spanish language in the Philippines">Spanish language in the Philippines</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:263px;max-width:263px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La-solidaridad2.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="367" data-file-width="264" decoding="async" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/La-solidaridad2.jpg/125px-La-solidaridad2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/La-solidaridad2.jpg/188px-La-solidaridad2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/La-solidaridad2.jpg/250px-La-solidaridad2.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:132px;max-width:132px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_Illustracion_Filipina_(1892).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="545" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg/130px-La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg/195px-La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg/260px-La_Illustracion_Filipina_%281892%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><i><a href="/wiki/La_Solidaridad" title="La Solidaridad">La Solidaridad</a></i> newspaper and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Luna" title="Juan Luna">Juan Luna</a> (a Filipino <i><a href="/wiki/Ilustrado" title="Ilustrado">Ilustrado</a></i>).</div></div></div></div>
<p>Spanish was an official language of the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> from the beginning of Spanish administration in 1565 to a constitutional change in 1973. During <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1521%E2%80%931898)" title="History of the Philippines (1521–1898)">Spanish colonization</a> (1565–1898), it was the language of government, trade, and education, and was spoken as a first language by Spaniards and educated Filipinos. In the mid-19th century, the colonial government set up a free public education system with Spanish as the medium of instruction. While this increased the use of Spanish throughout the islands and led to the formation of a class of Spanish-speaking intellectuals called the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilustrados" title="Ilustrados">Ilustrados</a></i>, only populations in urban areas or with places with a significant Spanish presence used the language on a daily basis or learned it as a second or third language. By the end of Spanish rule in 1898, only about 10% of the population had knowledge of Spanish, mostly those of Spanish descent or elite standing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite <a href="/wiki/Insular_Government_of_the_Philippine_Islands" title="Insular Government of the Philippine Islands">American administration of the Philippines</a> after the defeat of Spain in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a>, Spanish continued to be used in Philippine literature and press during the early years of American administration. Gradually however, the American government began promoting the use of English at the expense of Spanish, characterizing it as a negative influence of the past. Eventually, by the 1920s, English became the primary language of administration and education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Nevertheless, despite a significant decrease in influence and speakers, Spanish remained an official language of the Philippines upon independence in 1946, alongside English and <a href="/wiki/Filipino_language" title="Filipino language">Filipino</a>, a standardized version of <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bandera_03.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="510" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bandera_03.jpg/250px-Bandera_03.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bandera_03.jpg/375px-Bandera_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Bandera_03.jpg/500px-Bandera_03.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bandera_03.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Early flag of the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Revolutionary_Army" title="Philippine Revolutionary Army">Filipino revolutionaries</a> ("Long live the Philippine Republic!!!"). The first two constitutions were written in Spanish.</div></div></div>
<p>Spanish was briefly removed from official status in 1973 under the administration of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Marcos" title="Ferdinand Marcos">Ferdinand Marcos</a>, but regained official status two months later under Presidential Decree No. 155, dated 15 March 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> It remained an official language until 1987, with the ratification of the present constitution, in which it was re-designated as a voluntary and optional auxiliary language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In 2010, President <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo" title="Gloria Macapagal Arroyo">Gloria Macapagal Arroyo</a> encouraged the reintroduction of Spanish-language teaching in the Philippine education system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> However, the initiative failed to gain any traction, with the number of secondary schools at which the language is either a compulsory subject or offered as an elective remaining very limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Today, the actual number of proficient Spanish speakers is around 400,000, or under 0.5% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> There are some 20,000 students studying the language every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup>
</p><p>Aside from standard Spanish, a Spanish-based creole language called <a href="/wiki/Chavacano" title="Chavacano">Chavacano</a> developed in the southern Philippines. However, it is not mutually intelligible with Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The number of Chavacano-speakers was estimated at 1.2 million in 1996.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The local <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Philippines" title="Languages of the Philippines">languages of the Philippines</a> also retain significant Spanish influence, with many words derived from <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">Mexican Spanish</a>, owing to the administration of the islands by Spain through <a href="/wiki/New_Spain" title="New Spain">New Spain</a> until 1821, until direct governance from Madrid afterwards to 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oceania">Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg/220px-Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg/330px-Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg/440px-Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parque_Nacional_Rapa_Nui.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Announcement in Spanish on <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>, welcoming visitors to <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_National_Park" title="Rapa Nui National Park">Rapa Nui National Park</a></div></div></div>
<p>Spanish is the official and most spoken language on <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">Easter Island</a>, which is geographically part of <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesia</a> in Oceania and politically part of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. However, Easter Island's traditional language is <a href="/wiki/Rapa_Nui_language" title="Rapa Nui language">Rapa Nui</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Eastern Polynesian language</a>.
</p><p>As a legacy of comprising the former <a href="/wiki/Spanish_East_Indies" title="Spanish East Indies">Spanish East Indies</a>, Spanish loan words are present in the local languages of <a href="/wiki/Guam" title="Guam">Guam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Micronesia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p><p><br/>
In addition, in Australia and New Zealand, there are native Spanish communities, resulting from emigration from Spanish-speaking countries. Mainly from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Cone" title="Southern Cone">Southern Cone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_speakers_by_country">Spanish speakers by country</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Spanish speakers by country">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">Grammar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Grammar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_grammar" title="Spanish grammar">Spanish grammar</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1893" data-file-width="1443" decoding="async" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg/170px-Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg/255px-Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg/340px-Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cervantes_J%C3%A1uregui.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a>, considered by many the greatest author of Spanish literature, and author of <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Quixote" title="Don Quixote">Don Quixote</a></i>, widely considered the first modern European novel.</div></div></div>
<p>Most of the grammatical and <a href="/wiki/Linguistic_typology" title="Linguistic typology">typological</a> features of Spanish are shared with the other <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>. Spanish is a <a href="/wiki/Fusional_language" title="Fusional language">fusional language</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nouns" title="Spanish nouns">noun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_adjectives" title="Spanish adjectives">adjective</a> systems exhibit two <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">genders</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">numbers</a>. In addition, articles and some <a href="/wiki/Spanish_pronouns" title="Spanish pronouns">pronouns</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_determiners" title="Spanish determiners">determiners</a> have a neuter gender in their singular form. There are about fifty <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_conjugation" title="Grammatical conjugation">conjugated</a> forms per <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">verb</a>, with 3 tenses: past, present, future; 2 <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">aspects</a> for past: <a href="/wiki/Perfective_aspect" title="Perfective aspect">perfective</a>, <a href="/wiki/Imperfective_aspect" title="Imperfective aspect">imperfective</a>; 4 <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">moods</a>: indicative, subjunctive, conditional, imperative; 3 persons: first, second, third; 2 numbers: singular, plural; 3 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Verboid" title="Verboid">verboid</a> forms: infinitive, gerund, and past participle. The indicative mood is the <a href="/wiki/Markedness" title="Markedness">unmarked</a> one, while the subjunctive mood expresses uncertainty or indetermination, and is commonly paired with the conditional, which is a mood used to express "would" (as in, "I would eat if I had food); the imperative is a mood to express a command, commonly a one word phrase – "¡Di!", "¡Talk!".
</p><p>Verbs express <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-V_distinction" title="T-V distinction">T-V distinction</a> by using different persons for formal and informal addresses. (For a detailed overview of verbs, see <a href="/wiki/Spanish_verbs" title="Spanish verbs">Spanish verbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_irregular_verbs" title="Spanish irregular verbs">Spanish irregular verbs</a>.)
</p><p>Spanish <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a> is considered <a href="/wiki/Branching_(linguistics)" title="Branching (linguistics)">right-branching</a>, meaning that subordinate or <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_modifier" title="Grammatical modifier">modifying</a> <a href="/wiki/Constituent_(linguistics)" title="Constituent (linguistics)">constituents</a> tend to be placed after head words. The language uses <a href="/wiki/Preposition_and_postposition" title="Preposition and postposition">prepositions</a> (rather than postpositions or inflection of nouns for <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">case</a>), and usually—though not always—places <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">adjectives</a> after <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">nouns</a>, as do most other Romance languages.
</p><p>Spanish is classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93verb%E2%80%93object" title="Subject–verb–object">subject–verb–object</a> language; however, as in most Romance languages, constituent order is highly variable and governed mainly by <a href="/wiki/Topicalization" title="Topicalization">topicalization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Focus_(linguistics)" title="Focus (linguistics)">focus</a> rather than by syntax. It is a "<a href="/wiki/Pro-drop_language" title="Pro-drop language">pro-drop</a>", or "<a href="/wiki/Null-subject_language" title="Null-subject language">null-subject</a>" language—that is, it allows the deletion of subject pronouns when they are <a href="/wiki/Pragmatics" title="Pragmatics">pragmatically</a> unnecessary. Spanish is described as a "<a href="/wiki/Verb_framing" title="Verb framing">verb-framed</a>" language, meaning that the <i>direction</i> of motion is expressed in the verb while the <i>mode</i> of locomotion is expressed adverbially (e.g. <i>subir corriendo</i> or <i>salir volando</i>; the respective English equivalents of these examples—'to run up' and 'to fly out'—show that English is, by contrast, "satellite-framed", with mode of locomotion expressed in the verb and direction in an adverbial modifier).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><audio class="thumbimage" controls="" data-durationhint="11" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" data-mwtitle="Miguel_Hache_-_voice.ogg" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px;" width="220"><source data-bandwidth="228408" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-title="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Miguel_Hache_-_voice.ogg/Miguel_Hache_-_voice.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg"/><source data-bandwidth="423701" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (424 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Miguel_Hache_-_voice.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'/></audio> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Miguel_Hache_-_voice.ogg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish spoken in Spain</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology" title="Spanish phonology">Spanish phonology</a></div>
<p>The Spanish phonological system evolved from that of <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a>. Its development exhibits some traits in common with other <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">Western Romance languages</a>, others with the neighboring Hispanic varieties—especially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leonese_dialect" title="Leonese dialect">Leonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_language" title="Aragonese language">Aragonese</a>—as well as other features unique to Spanish. Spanish is alone among its immediate neighbors in having undergone frequent aspiration and eventual loss of the Latin initial <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span> sound (e.g. Cast. <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">harina</i></span> vs. Leon. and Arag. <span title="Asturian-language text"><i lang="ast">farina</i></span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> The Latin initial consonant sequences <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">pl-</i></span>, <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">cl-</i></span>, and <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">fl-</i></span> in Spanish typically merge as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ll-</i></span> (originally pronounced <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʎ]</span>), while in Aragonese they are preserved in most dialects, and in Leonese they present a variety of outcomes, including <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[tʃ]</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʃ]</span>, and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʎ]</span>. Where Latin had <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">-li-</i></span> before a vowel (e.g. <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">filius</i></span>) or the ending <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">-iculus</i></span>, <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">-icula</i></span> (e.g. <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">auricula</i></span>), Old Spanish produced <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʒ]</span>, that in Modern Spanish became the velar fricative <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[x]</span> (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">hijo</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">oreja</i></span>), whereas neighboring languages have the palatal lateral <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʎ]</span> (e.g. Portuguese <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">filho</i></span>, <span title="Portuguese-language text"><i lang="pt">orelha</i></span>; Catalan <span title="Catalan-language text"><i lang="ca">fill</i></span>, <span title="Catalan-language text"><i lang="ca">orella</i></span>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Segmental_phonology">Segmental phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Segmental phonology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vowel_chart.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="746" data-file-width="982" decoding="async" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/250px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/375px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Spanish_vowel_chart.svg/500px-Spanish_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spanish_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spanish vowel chart, from <a href="#CITEREFLadefogedJohnson2010">Ladefoged &amp; Johnson (2010</a>:227)</div></div></div>
<p>The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemic</a> inventory consists of five vowel phonemes (<span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>) and 17 to 19 consonant phonemes (the exact number depending on the dialect<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>). The main <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophonic</a> variation among vowels is the reduction of the high vowels <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> to glides—<span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[j]</span> and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[w]</span> respectively—when unstressed and adjacent to another vowel. Some instances of the mid vowels <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span> and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span>, determined lexically, alternate with the diphthongs <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/je/</span> and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/we/</span> respectively when stressed, in a process that is better described as <a href="/wiki/Morphophonology" title="Morphophonology">morphophonemic</a> rather than phonological, as it is not predictable from phonology alone.
</p><p>The Spanish consonant system is characterized by (1) three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">nasal</a> phonemes, and one or two (depending on the dialect) <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">lateral</a> phoneme(s), which in syllable-final position <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archiphonemic" title="Archiphonemic">lose their contrast</a> and are subject to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assimilation_(linguistics)" title="Assimilation (linguistics)">assimilation</a> to a following consonant; (2) three <a href="/wiki/Voicelessness" title="Voicelessness">voiceless</a> <a href="/wiki/Plosive" title="Plosive">stops</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">affricate</a> <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>; (3) three or four (depending on the dialect) <a href="/wiki/Voicelessness" title="Voicelessness">voiceless</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">fricatives</a>; (4) a set of voiced <a href="/wiki/Obstruent" title="Obstruent">obstruents</a>—<span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span>, and sometimes <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʝ/</span>—which alternate between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">approximant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Plosive" title="Plosive">plosive</a> allophones depending on the environment; and (5) a phonemic distinction between the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">tapped</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">trilled</a>" <i>r</i>-sounds (single ⟨r⟩ and double ⟨rr⟩ in orthography).
</p><p>In the following table of consonant phonemes, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span> is marked with an asterisk (*) to indicate that it is preserved only in some dialects. In most dialects it has been merged with <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʝ/</span> in the merger called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a href="/wiki/Ye%C3%ADsmo" title="Yeísmo">yeísmo</a></i></span>. Similarly, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span> is also marked with an asterisk to indicate that most dialects do not distinguish it from <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> (see <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seseo" title="Seseo">seseo</a></i></span>), although this is not a true merger but an outcome of different evolution of sibilants in Southern Spain.
</p><p>The phoneme <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> is in parentheses () to indicate that it appears only in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loanwords" title="Loanwords">loanwords</a>. Each of the voiced obstruent phonemes <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʝ/</span>, and <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> appears to the right of a <i>pair</i> of voiceless phonemes, to indicate that, while the <i>voiceless</i> phonemes maintain a phonemic contrast between plosive (or affricate) and fricative, the <i>voiced</i> ones alternate <a href="/wiki/Allophone" title="Allophone">allophonically</a> (i.e. without phonemic contrast) between plosive and approximant pronunciations.
</p>

</td>
<td style="border-right: 0;"><span class="IPA" lang="und-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_fricative" title="Voiceless dental fricative">θ</a></span>*
