</tr><tr><td class="sidebar-navbar" style="border-top:1px solid #aaa; padding-bottom:0.4em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1063604349">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar a>span,.mw-parser-output .navbar a>abbr{text-decoration:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}</style><div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Spanish_language" title="Template:Spanish language"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Spanish_language" title="Template talk:Spanish language"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Spanish_language&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Spanish is written in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a>, with the addition of the character ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">ñ</a>⟩ (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">eñe</i></span>, representing the phoneme <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palatal_nasal" title="Palatal nasal">ɲ</a>/</span>, a letter distinct from ⟨n⟩, although typographically composed of an ⟨n⟩ with a <a href="/wiki/Tilde" title="Tilde">tilde</a>). Formerly the <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">digraphs</a> ⟨ch⟩ (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">che</i></span>, representing the phoneme <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ʃ/</span>) and ⟨ll⟩ (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">elle</i></span>, representing the phoneme <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">ʎ</a>/</span> or <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʝ/</span>), were also considered single letters. However, the digraph ⟨rr⟩ (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">erre fuerte</i></span>, 'strong r', <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">erre doble</i></span>, 'double r', or simply <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">erre</i></span>), which also represents a distinct phoneme <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r/</span>, was not similarly regarded as a single letter. Since 1994 ⟨ch⟩ and ⟨ll⟩ have been treated as letter pairs for <a href="/wiki/Collation" title="Collation">collation</a> purposes, though they remained a part of the alphabet until 2010. Words with ⟨ch⟩ are now alphabetically sorted between those with ⟨cg⟩ and ⟨ci⟩, instead of following ⟨cz⟩ as they used to. The situation is similar for ⟨ll⟩.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup>
</p><p>Thus, the Spanish alphabet has the following 27 letters:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">A, B, C, D, E, F, G, H, I, J, K, L, M, N, Ñ, O, P, Q, R,  S, T, U, V, W, X, Y, Z.</i></span></dd></dl>
<p>Since 2010, none of the digraphs (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ch, ll, rr, gu, qu</i></span>) are considered letters by the Royal Spanish Academy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup>
</p><p>The letters <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">k</i></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">w</i></span> are used only in words and names coming from foreign languages (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">kilo, folklore, whisky, kiwi</i></span>, etc.).
</p><p>With the exclusion of a very small number of regional terms such as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%A9xico" title="México">México</a></i></span> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toponymy_of_Mexico#Phonetic_evolution" title="Toponymy of Mexico">Toponymy of Mexico</a>), pronunciation can be entirely determined from spelling. Under the orthographic conventions, a typical Spanish word is stressed on the <a href="/wiki/Syllable" title="Syllable">syllable</a> before the last if it ends with a vowel (not including ⟨y⟩) or with a vowel followed by ⟨n⟩ or an ⟨s⟩; it is stressed on the last syllable otherwise. Exceptions to this rule are indicated by placing an <a href="/wiki/Acute_accent" title="Acute accent">acute accent</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">stressed vowel</a>.
</p><p>The acute accent is used, in addition, to distinguish between certain <a href="/wiki/Homophone" title="Homophone">homophones</a>, especially when one of them is a stressed word and the other one is a <a href="/wiki/Clitic" title="Clitic">clitic</a>: compare <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">el</i></span> ('the', masculine singular definite article) with <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">él</i></span> ('he' or 'it'), or <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">te</i></span> ('you', object pronoun) with <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">té</i></span> ('tea'), <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">de</i></span> (preposition 'of') versus <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">dé</i></span> ('give' [formal imperative/third-person present subjunctive]), and <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">se</i></span> (reflexive pronoun) versus <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sé</i></span> ('I know' or imperative 'be').
</p><p>The interrogative pronouns (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">qué</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">cuál</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">dónde</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">quién</i></span>, etc.) also receive accents in direct or indirect questions, and some demonstratives (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ése</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">éste</i></span>, <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">aquél</i></span>, etc.) can be accented when used as pronouns. Accent marks used to be omitted on capital letters (a widespread practice in the days of <a href="/wiki/Typewriter" title="Typewriter">typewriters</a> and the early days of computers when only lowercase vowels were available with accents), although the <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Real Academia Española</i></span> advises against this and the orthographic conventions taught at schools enforce the use of the accent.
</p><p>When <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">u</i></span> is written between <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">g</i></span> and a front vowel <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">e</i></span> or <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">i</i></span>, it indicates a "<a href="/wiki/Hard_and_soft_G" title="Hard and soft G">hard g</a>" pronunciation. A <a href="/wiki/Diaeresis_(diacritic)" title="Diaeresis (diacritic)">diaeresis</a> <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ü</i></span> indicates that it is not silent as it normally would be (e.g., <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">cigüeña</i></span>, 'stork', is pronounced <span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[θiˈɣweɲa]</span>; if it were written *<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">cigueña</i></span>, it would be pronounced *<span class="IPA" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[θiˈɣeɲa]</span>).
</p><p>Interrogative and exclamatory clauses are introduced with <a href="/wiki/Inverted_question_and_exclamation_marks" title="Inverted question and exclamation marks">inverted question and exclamation marks</a> (<span title="Spanish-language text"><span lang="es">¿</span></span> and <span title="Spanish-language text"><span lang="es">¡</span></span>, respectively) and closed by the usual question and exclamation marks.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations">Organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:62px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1036" data-file-width="746" decoding="async" height="83" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg/60px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg/90px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg/120px-Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg.png 2x" width="60"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_Arms_of_the_Royal_Spanish_Academy.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arms of the Royal Spanish Academy</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="422" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg/220px-Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg/330px-Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg/440px-Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Academia_de_la_Lengua.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Royal Spanish Academy Headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Spanish_Academy">Royal Spanish Academy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Royal Spanish Academy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Academy" title="Royal Spanish Academy">Royal Spanish Academy</a></div>
<p>The Royal Spanish Academy (<a class="mw-selflink selflink">Spanish</a>: <i lang="es">Real Academia Española</i>), founded in 1713,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> together with the 21 other national ones (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Spanish_Language_Academies" title="Association of Spanish Language Academies">Association of Spanish Language Academies</a>), exercises a standardizing influence through its publication of dictionaries and widely respected grammar and style guides.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup>
Because of influence and for other sociohistorical reasons, a standardized form of the language (<a href="/wiki/Standard_Spanish" title="Standard Spanish">Standard Spanish</a>) is widely acknowledged for use in literature, academic contexts and the media.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Association_of_Spanish_Language_Academies">Association of Spanish Language Academies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Association of Spanish Language Academies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_Spanish_Language_Academies" title="Association of Spanish Language Academies">Association of Spanish Language Academies</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1398" data-file-width="2754" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg/220px-Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg/330px-Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg/440px-Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pa%C3%ADses_con_Academia_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries members of the ASALE.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The Association of Spanish Language Academies (<span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Asociación de Academias de la Lengua Española</i></span>, or <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">ASALE</i></span>) is the entity which regulates the Spanish language. It was created in Mexico in 1951 and represents the union of all the separate academies in the Spanish-speaking world. It comprises the academies of 23 countries, ordered by date of Academy foundation: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Academia_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Real Academia Española">Spain</a> (1713),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Colombiana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Colombiana de la Lengua">Colombia</a> (1871),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Ecuatoriana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Ecuatoriana de la Lengua">Ecuador</a> (1874),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[247]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Mexicana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Mexicana de la Lengua">Mexico</a> (1875),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Salvadore%C3%B1a_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Salvadoreña de la Lengua">El Salvador</a> (1876),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Venezolana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Venezolana de la Lengua">Venezuela</a> (1883),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Chilena_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Chilena de la Lengua">Chile</a> (1885),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia_Peruana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Peruana de la Lengua">Peru</a> (1887),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Guatemalteca_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Guatemalteca de la Lengua">Guatemala</a> (1887),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Costarricense_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Costarricense de la Lengua">Costa Rica</a> (1923),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia_Filipina_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Academia Filipina de la Lengua Española">Philippines</a> (1924),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Paname%C3%B1a_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Panameña de la Lengua">Panama</a> (1926),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Cubana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Cubana de la Lengua">Cuba</a> (1926),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Academia_Paraguaya_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Academia Paraguaya de la Lengua Española">Paraguay</a> (1927),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Dominicana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Dominicana de la Lengua">Dominican Republic</a> (1927),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Boliviana_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Boliviana de la Lengua">Bolivia</a> (1927),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Nicarag%C3%BCense_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Nicaragüense de la Lengua">Nicaragua</a> (1928),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Argentina_de_Letras" title="Academia Argentina de Letras">Argentina</a> (1931),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academia_Nacional_de_Letras,_del_Uruguay" title="Academia Nacional de Letras, del Uruguay">Uruguay</a> (1943),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Hondure%C3%B1a_de_la_Lengua" title="Academia Hondureña de la Lengua">Honduras</a> (1949),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Academia_Puertorrique%C3%B1a_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Academia Puertorriqueña de la Lengua Española">Puerto Rico</a> (1955),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_American_Academy_of_the_Spanish_Language" title="North American Academy of the Spanish Language">United States</a> (1973)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Academia_Ecuatoguineana_de_la_Lengua_Espa%C3%B1ola" title="Academia Ecuatoguineana de la Lengua Española">Equatorial Guinea</a> (2016).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cervantes_Institute">Cervantes Institute</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Cervantes Institute">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Cervantes" title="Instituto Cervantes">Instituto Cervantes</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Madrid)_05.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2515" data-file-width="2078" decoding="async" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg/170px-Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg/255px-Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg/340px-Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_%28Madrid%29_05.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banco_Espa%C3%B1ol_del_R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata_(Madrid)_05.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cervantes_Institute" title="Cervantes Institute">Cervantes Institute</a> headquarters, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Instituto Cervantes</i></span> (Cervantes Institute) is a worldwide nonprofit organization created by the Spanish government in 1991. This organization has branches in 45 countries, with 88 centers devoted to the Spanish and Hispanic American cultures and Spanish language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> The goals of the Institute are to promote universally the education, the study, and the use of Spanish as a second language, to support methods and activities that help the process of Spanish-language education, and to contribute to the advancement of the Spanish and Hispanic American cultures in non-Spanish-speaking countries. The institute's 2015 report "El español, una lengua viva" (Spanish, a living language) estimated that there were 559 million Spanish speakers worldwide. Its latest annual report "<a class="external text" href="https://www.cervantes.es/sobre_instituto_cervantes/prensa/2018/noticias/np_presentacion-anuario.htm" rel="nofollow">El español en el mundo 2018</a>" (Spanish in the world 2018) counts 577 million Spanish speakers worldwide. Among the sources cited in the report is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a>, which estimates that the U.S. will have 138 million Spanish speakers by 2050, making it the biggest Spanish-speaking nation on earth, with Spanish the mother tongue of almost a third of its citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_use_by_international_organizations">Official use by international organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Official use by international organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a more comprehensive list, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_where_Spanish_is_an_official_language#International_organizations_where_Spanish_is_official" title="List of countries where Spanish is an official language">List of countries where Spanish is an official language § International organizations where Spanish is official</a>.</div>
<p>Spanish is one of the official languages of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_American_States" title="Organization of American States">Organization of American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_Ibero-American_States" title="Organization of Ibero-American States">Organization of Ibero-American States</a>, the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_American_Nations" title="Union of South American Nations">Union of South American Nations</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_Secretariat" title="Antarctic Treaty Secretariat">Antarctic Treaty Secretariat</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Latin_Union" title="Latin Union">Latin Union</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caricom" title="Caricom">Caricom</a>, the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Inter-American_Development_Bank" title="Inter-American Development Bank">Inter-American Development Bank</a>, and numerous other international organizations.
</p>
<div style="clear:right;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Sample text">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Article 1 of the <i><a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a></i> in Spanish:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Todos los seres humanos nacen libres e iguales en dignidad y derechos y, dotados como están de razón y conciencia, deben comportarse fraternalmente los unos con los otros.</i></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Article 1 of the <i>Universal Declaration of Human Rights</i> in English:
</p>
<dl><dd><i>All human beings are born free and equal in dignity and rights. They are endowed with reason and conscience and should act towards one another in a spirit of brotherhood.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup></dd></dl>

<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">According to Ethnologue (see <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://www.ethnologue.com/country/AR/languages" rel="nofollow">"Argentina"</a>. <i>Ethnologue</i></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Ethnologue&amp;rft.atitle=Argentina&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ethnologue.com%2Fcountry%2FAR%2Flanguages&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASpanish+language"></span>), there were 40,3 million speakers Spanish as mother tongue in 2013. The Argentinian population in 2013 was projected to be 42,2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-proyecciones_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-proyecciones-95">[95]</a></sup></span>

<li id="cite_note-236"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-236">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="#CITEREFPenny1991">Penny (1991</a>:224–236)</span>

<li id="cite_note-237"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-237">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Often considered to be a substratum word. Other theories suggest, on the basis of what is used to make cheese, a derivation from Latin <i>brandeum</i> (originally meaning a linen covering, later a thin cloth for relic storage) through an intermediate root *<i>brandea</i>. For the development of the meaning, cf. Spanish <i>manteca</i>, Portuguese <i>manteiga</i>, probably from Latin <i>mantica</i> ('sack'), Italian <i>formaggio</i> and French <i>fromage</i> from <i>formaticus</i>. <a class="external text" href="http://dexonline.ro./definitie/brânză" rel="nofollow">Romanian Explanatory Dictionary</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20200218134722/https://dexonline.ro/definitie/br%C3%A2nz%C4%83" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 18 February 2020 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a></span>
</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="External_links">External links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Spanish_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: External links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dt>Organizations</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://www.rae.es/" rel="nofollow">Real Academia Española (RAE)</a>, Royal Spanish Academy. Spain's official institution, with a mission to ensure the stability of the Spanish language</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.cervantes.es/default.htm" rel="nofollow">Instituto Cervantes</a>, Cervantes Institute. A Spanish government agency, responsible for promoting the study and the teaching of the Spanish language and culture.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://www.fundeu.es/" rel="nofollow">FundéuRAE</a>, Foundation of Emerging Spanish. A non-profit organization with collaboration of the RAE which mission is to clarify doubts and ambiguities of Spanish.</li></ul>
<dl><dt>Educational websites</dt></dl>
<ul><li><a class="external text" href="https://profedeele.es" rel="nofollow">ProfeDeEle</a>, Exercises targeted toward Spanish language teachers (ELE)</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://aprenderespanol.org" rel="nofollow">AprenderEspanol</a>, Spanish activities and material</li></ul>
